House File 2441 - Introduced


                                 HOUSE FILE 

                                 HOUSE FILE 
                                 HOUSE FILE                                  HOUSE FILE                                  BY  WESSEL=KROESCHELL,
                                     HANSON, WINCKLER,
                                     HEDDENS, OURTH,
                                     KELLEY, and STAED

 A BILL FOR

  1 An Act providing for an increase in the maximum local option
  2    sales tax rate to fund local natural resources and outdoor
  3    recreation projects.
  4 BE IT ENACTED BY THE GENERAL ASSEMBLY OF THE STATE OF IOWA:
    TLSB 5556YH (3) 86
    mm/sc

PAG LIN



  1  1    Section 1.  Section 423B.1, subsection 5, Code 2016, is
  1  2 amended to read as follows:
  1  3    5.  The county commissioner of elections shall submit the
  1  4 question of imposition of a local option tax at an election
  1  5 held on a date specified in section 39.2, subsection 4,
  1  6 paragraph "a". The election shall not be held sooner than sixty
  1  7 days after publication of notice of the ballot proposition.
  1  8 The ballot proposition shall specify the type and rate of tax
  1  9 and in the case of a vehicle tax the classes that will be
  1 10 exempt and in the case of a local sales and services tax the
  1 11 date it will be imposed which date shall not be earlier than
  1 12 ninety days following the election. The ballot proposition
  1 13 shall also specify the approximate amount of local option tax
  1 14 revenues that will be used for property tax relief and shall
  1 15 contain a statement as to the specific purpose or purposes for
  1 16 which the revenues shall otherwise be expended. If the county
  1 17 board of supervisors decides under subsection 6 to specify a
  1 18 date on which the local option sales and services tax shall
  1 19 automatically be repealed, the date of the repeal shall also
  1 20 be specified on the ballot. The rate of the vehicle tax shall
  1 21 be in increments of one dollar per vehicle as set by the
  1 22 petition seeking to impose the tax. The rate of a local sales
  1 23 and services tax shall not be more than one                                      HANSON, WINCKLER,
                                     HEDDENS, OURTH,
                                     KELLEY, and STAED

  1  1    Section 1.  Section 423B.1, subsection 5, Code 2016, is
  1  2 amended to read as follows:
  1  3    5.  The county commissioner of elections shall submit the
  1  4 question of imposition of a local option tax at an election
  1  5 held on a date specified in section 39.2, subsection 4,
  1  6 paragraph "a". The election shall not be held sooner than sixty
  1  7 days after publication of notice of the ballot proposition.
  1  8 The ballot proposition shall specify the type and rate of tax
  1  9 and in the case of a vehicle tax the classes that will be
  1 10 exempt and in the case of a local sales and services tax the
  1 11 date it will be imposed which date shall not be earlier than
  1 12 ninety days following the election. The ballot proposition
  1 13 shall also specify the approximate amount of local option tax
  1 14 revenues that will be used for property tax relief and shall
  1 15 contain a statement as to the specific purpose or purposes for
  1 16 which the revenues shall otherwise be expended. If the county
  1 17 board of supervisors decides under subsection 6 to specify a
  1 18 date on which the local option sales and services tax shall
  1 19 automatically be repealed, the date of the repeal shall also
  1 20 be specified on the ballot. The rate of the vehicle tax shall
  1 21 be in increments of one dollar per vehicle as set by the
  1 22 petition seeking to impose the tax. The rate of a local sales
  1 23 and services tax shall not be more than one                                      HEDDENS, OURTH,

  1  1    Section 1.  Section 423B.1, subsection 5, Code 2016, is
  1  2 amended to read as follows:
  1  3    5.  The county commissioner of elections shall submit the
  1  4 question of imposition of a local option tax at an election
  1  5 held on a date specified in section 39.2, subsection 4,
  1  6 paragraph "a". The election shall not be held sooner than sixty
  1  7 days after publication of notice of the ballot proposition.
  1  8 The ballot proposition shall specify the type and rate of tax
  1  9 and in the case of a vehicle tax the classes that will be
  1 10 exempt and in the case of a local sales and services tax the
  1 11 date it will be imposed which date shall not be earlier than
  1 12 ninety days following the election. The ballot proposition
  1 13 shall also specify the approximate amount of local option tax
  1 14 revenues that will be used for property tax relief and shall
  1 15 contain a statement as to the specific purpose or purposes for
  1 16 which the revenues shall otherwise be expended. If the county
  1 17 board of supervisors decides under subsection 6 to specify a
  1 18 date on which the local option sales and services tax shall
  1 19 automatically be repealed, the date of the repeal shall also
  1 20 be specified on the ballot. The rate of the vehicle tax shall
  1 21 be in increments of one dollar per vehicle as set by the
  1 22 petition seeking to impose the tax. The rate of a local sales
  1 23 and services tax shall not be more than one   2    sales tax rate to fund local natural resources and outdoor

  2  6 II. A local sales and services tax shall be imposed on the
  2  7 same basis as the state sales and services tax or in the case
  2  8 of the use of natural gas, natural gas service, electricity,
  2  9 or electric service on the same basis as the state use tax
  2 10 and shall not be imposed on the sale of any property or on
  2 11 any service not taxed by the state, except the tax shall not
  2 12 be imposed on the sales price from the sale of motor fuel
  2 13 or special fuel as defined in chapter 452A which is consumed
  2 14 for highway use or in watercraft or aircraft if the fuel tax
  2 15 is paid on the transaction and a refund has not or will not
  2 16 be allowed, on the sales price from the sale of equipment by
  2 17 the state department of transportation, or on the sales price
  2 18 from the sale or use of natural gas, natural gas service,
  2 19 electricity, or electric service in a city or county where the
  2 20 sales price from the sale of natural gas or electric energy is
  2 21 subject to a franchise fee or user fee during the period the
  2 22 franchise or user fee is imposed. A local sales and services
  2 23 tax is applicable to transactions within those incorporated
  2 24 and unincorporated areas of the county where it is imposed and
  2 25 shall be collected by all persons required to collect state
  2 26 sales taxes. All cities contiguous to each other shall be
  2 27 treated as part of one incorporated area and the tax would be
  2 28 imposed in each of those contiguous cities only if the majority
  2 29 of those voting in the total area covered by the contiguous
  2 30 cities favors its imposition. In the case of a local sales and
  2 31 services tax submitted to the registered voters of two or more
  2 32 contiguous counties as provided in section 423B.1, subsection
  2 33 4, paragraph "c", all cities contiguous to each other shall be
  2 34 treated as part of one incorporated area, even if the corporate
  2 35 boundaries of one or more of the cities include areas of more
  3  1 than one county, and the tax shall be imposed in each of those
  3  2 contiguous cities only if a majority of those voting on the tax
  3  3 in the total area covered by the contiguous cities favored its
  3  4 imposition.

  4 25 ordinance authorized under subsection 2, an eligible city

  4 28 423B.7, subsections 3, 4, and 5, to the special fund described

  4 29 in section 403.19, subsection 2  4 29 in section 403.19, subsection 2  4 30 services tax revenue deposited in the special fund of a city or
  4 31 county pursuant to section 423B.7, subsection 6A  4 31 county pursuant to section 423B.7, subsection 6A  4 32    Sec. 9.    4 33 outdoor recreation projects.
  4 34    1.  Moneys deposited in a special fund of a city or county
  4 35 pursuant to section 423B.7, subsection 6A, shall be used by
  5  1 the city or county only as provided in this section and only
  5  2 to support voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for
  5  3 regulatory efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.
  5  4    2.  In addition to the moneys deposited pursuant to section
  5  5 423B.7, subsection 6A, a city or county may deposit any other
  5  6 local sales and services tax revenues received by it pursuant
  5  7 to the distribution formula in section 423B.7, subsections 3,
  5  8 4, and 5.
  5  9    3.  Two or more cities or counties may enter into an
  5 10 agreement under chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  5 11 out any initiative described in this section.
  5 12    4.  Twenty=three percent of the moneys in each fund shall be
  5 13 used to support the following initiatives:
  5 14    a.  The establishment, restoration, or enhancement of parks,
  5 15 preserves, forests, wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native
  5 16 prairies, and wetlands.
  5 17    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  5 18    c.  Recreational purposes.
  5 19    d.  Technical assistance and financial incentives to private
  5 20 landowners to promote the management of forests, fisheries,
  5 21 wetlands, and wildlife.
  5 22    e.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  5 23    f.  Education and outreach that provide instruction regarding
  5 24 natural history and the outdoors. The subjects of such
  5 25 instruction may relate to opportunities involving recreational
  5 26 purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  5 27    5.  Twenty percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  5 28 to support the following initiatives:
  5 29    a.  Soil conservation and watershed protection.
  5 30    b.  The conservation of highly erodible land.
  5 31    c.  Soil conservation or crop management practices used on
  5 32 land producing biomass for biorefineries, including cellulosic
  5 33 ethanol production.
  5 34    6.  Fourteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  5 35 to support the following initiatives:
  6  1    a.  Water resource projects to preserve watersheds, including
  6  2 but not limited to all of the following:
  6  3    (1)  Projects to protect, restore, or enhance water
  6  4 quality through the provision of financial assistance for
  6  5 impairment=based, locally directed watershed projects,
  6  6 including water resource restoration projects as defined in
  6  7 section 384.80.
  6  8    (2)  Regional and community watershed assessment, planning,
  6  9 and prioritization efforts, including as provided in chapter
  6 10 466B.
  6 11    b.  Surface water protection projects and practices,
  6 12 including but not limited to the installation of permanent
  6 13 vegetation cover, filter strips, grass waterways, and riparian
  6 14 forest buffers; dredging; and bank stabilization.
  6 15    7.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  6 16 as follows:
  6 17    a.  Fifty=two percent shall be used to support initiatives
  6 18 involving the acquisition, protection, and development of
  6 19 parks, preserves, and open spaces, including multipurpose
  6 20 trails, restroom facilities, shelter houses, and picnic
  6 21 facilities, but excluding athletic fields, baseball or softball
  6 22 diamonds, tennis courts, golf courses, swimming pools, and
  6 23 other sport facilities.
  6 24    b.  Twenty percent shall be used to support the same
  6 25 initiatives listed in subsection 8.
  6 26    c.  Twenty percent shall be used to support soil and water
  6 27 enhancement programs, including but not limited to woodland
  6 28 protection and enhancement, wildlife habitat preservation and
  6 29 enhancement, protection of highly erodible soils, and clean
  6 30 water.
  6 31    d.  Five percent shall be used to support historical resource
  6 32 development programs.
  6 33    e.  Three percent shall be used for the development and
  6 34 implementation of integrated roadside vegetation plans.
  6 35    8.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7  1 to support the following initiatives:
  7  2    a.  The maintenance and improvement of parks, preserves,
  7  3 wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native prairies, and
  7  4 wetlands.
  7  5    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  7  6    c.  Recreational purposes.
  7  7    d.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  7  8    e.  Education and outreach programs and projects that provide
  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 14 to support initiatives related to the design, establishment,
  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.
  7 22                           EXPLANATION
  7 23 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  7 24 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  7 25    This bill provides for an increase in the maximum local
  7 26 option sales tax rate to fund local natural resources and
  7 27 outdoor recreation projects.
  7 28    BACKGROUND.  Under current law, counties may impose a sales
  7 29 tax at the local level upon a petition of the voters or motions
  7 30 of city councils or the board of supervisors and after an
  7 31 election at which a majority of those voting favors imposition.
  7 32 A majority vote is also required for a repeal or rate change,
  7 33 but the governing body on its own motion may repeal the sales
  7 34 tax under certain circumstances.  The local option sales tax
  7 35 rate may not exceed one percent.
  8  1 Local option tax revenues collected in a county are remitted
  8  2 to the department of revenue (department) and, except for
  8  3 certain revenues attributable to urban renewal projects,
  8  4 distributed back to the county and cities within the county
  8  5 using a statutory formula involving population and historical
  8  6 property tax revenues.
  8  7    BILL CHANGES.  The bill increases the maximum local option
  8  8 sales tax rate that may be imposed by a county to one and
  8  9 three=eighths percent (1.375 percent) from one percent.  If a
  8 10 county votes to initially impose or to increase the tax rate
  8 11 above one percent, the bill requires tax revenues collected
  8 12 on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one percent to be
  8 13 remitted to counties and cities using the existing statutory
  8 14 formula, and then deposited in a special fund of the city or
  8 15 county and used exclusively for funding natural resources and
  8 16 outdoor recreation projects as described in the bill.
  8 17    The special fund moneys shall only be used to support
  8 18 voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for regulatory
  8 19 efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.  The bill allows
  8 20 for two or more cities or counties to enter into an agreement
  8 21 under Code chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  8 22 out any authorized initiative, and allows a city or county to
  8 23 deposit other local sales and services tax revenues it receives
  8 24 in its special natural resources and outdoor recreation fund.
  8 25    The bill also amends the calculation for determining
  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.
       LSB 5556YH (3) 86

  6 22 diamonds, tennis courts, golf courses, swimming pools, and
  6 23 other sport facilities.
  6 24    b.  Twenty percent shall be used to support the same
  6 25 initiatives listed in subsection 8.
  6 26    c.  Twenty percent shall be used to support soil and water
  6 27 enhancement programs, including but not limited to woodland
  6 28 protection and enhancement, wildlife habitat preservation and
  6 29 enhancement, protection of highly erodible soils, and clean
  6 30 water.
  6 31    d.  Five percent shall be used to support historical resource
  6 32 development programs.
  6 33    e.  Three percent shall be used for the development and
  6 34 implementation of integrated roadside vegetation plans.
  6 35    8.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7  1 to support the following initiatives:
  7  2    a.  The maintenance and improvement of parks, preserves,
  7  3 wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native prairies, and
  7  4 wetlands.
  7  5    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  7  6    c.  Recreational purposes.
  7  7    d.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  7  8    e.  Education and outreach programs and projects that provide
  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 14 to support initiatives related to the design, establishment,
  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.
  7 22                           EXPLANATION
  7 23 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  7 24 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  7 25    This bill provides for an increase in the maximum local
  7 26 option sales tax rate to fund local natural resources and
  7 27 outdoor recreation projects.
  7 28    BACKGROUND.  Under current law, counties may impose a sales
  7 29 tax at the local level upon a petition of the voters or motions
  7 30 of city councils or the board of supervisors and after an
  7 31 election at which a majority of those voting favors imposition.
  7 32 A majority vote is also required for a repeal or rate change,
  7 33 but the governing body on its own motion may repeal the sales
  7 34 tax under certain circumstances.  The local option sales tax
  7 35 rate may not exceed one percent.
  8  1 Local option tax revenues collected in a county are remitted
  8  2 to the department of revenue (department) and, except for
  8  3 certain revenues attributable to urban renewal projects,
  8  4 distributed back to the county and cities within the county
  8  5 using a statutory formula involving population and historical
  8  6 property tax revenues.
  8  7    BILL CHANGES.  The bill increases the maximum local option
  8  8 sales tax rate that may be imposed by a county to one and
  8  9 three=eighths percent (1.375 percent) from one percent.  If a
  8 10 county votes to initially impose or to increase the tax rate
  8 11 above one percent, the bill requires tax revenues collected
  8 12 on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one percent to be
  8 13 remitted to counties and cities using the existing statutory
  8 14 formula, and then deposited in a special fund of the city or
  8 15 county and used exclusively for funding natural resources and
  8 16 outdoor recreation projects as described in the bill.
  8 17    The special fund moneys shall only be used to support
  8 18 voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for regulatory
  8 19 efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.  The bill allows
  8 20 for two or more cities or counties to enter into an agreement
  8 21 under Code chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  8 22 out any authorized initiative, and allows a city or county to
  8 23 deposit other local sales and services tax revenues it receives
  8 24 in its special natural resources and outdoor recreation fund.
  8 25    The bill also amends the calculation for determining
  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.
       LSB 5556YH (3) 86
       mm/sc
  5  2 to support voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for
  5  3 regulatory efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.
  5  4    2.  In addition to the moneys deposited pursuant to section
  5  5 423B.7, subsection 6A, a city or county may deposit any other
  5  6 local sales and services tax revenues received by it pursuant
  5  7 to the distribution formula in section 423B.7, subsections 3,
  5  8 4, and 5.
  5  9    3.  Two or more cities or counties may enter into an
  5 10 agreement under chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  5 11 out any initiative described in this section.
  5 12    4.  Twenty=three percent of the moneys in each fund shall be
  5 13 used to support the following initiatives:
  5 14    a.  The establishment, restoration, or enhancement of parks,
  5 15 preserves, forests, wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native
  5 16 prairies, and wetlands.
  5 17    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  5 18    c.  Recreational purposes.
  5 19    d.  Technical assistance and financial incentives to private
  5 20 landowners to promote the management of forests, fisheries,
  5 21 wetlands, and wildlife.
  5 22    e.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  5 23    f.  Education and outreach that provide instruction regarding
  5 24 natural history and the outdoors. The subjects of such
  5 25 instruction may relate to opportunities involving recreational
  5 26 purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  5 27    5.  Twenty percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  5 28 to support the following initiatives:
  5 29    a.  Soil conservation and watershed protection.
  5 30    b.  The conservation of highly erodible land.
  5 31    c.  Soil conservation or crop management practices used on
  5 32 land producing biomass for biorefineries, including cellulosic
  5 33 ethanol production.
  5 34    6.  Fourteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  5 35 to support the following initiatives:
  6  1    a.  Water resource projects to preserve watersheds, including
  6  2 but not limited to all of the following:
  6  3    (1)  Projects to protect, restore, or enhance water
  6  4 quality through the provision of financial assistance for
  6  5 impairment=based, locally directed watershed projects,
  6  6 including water resource restoration projects as defined in
  6  7 section 384.80.
  6  8    (2)  Regional and community watershed assessment, planning,
  6  9 and prioritization efforts, including as provided in chapter
  6 10 466B.
  6 11    b.  Surface water protection projects and practices,
  6 12 including but not limited to the installation of permanent
  6 13 vegetation cover, filter strips, grass waterways, and riparian
  6 14 forest buffers; dredging; and bank stabilization.
  6 15    7.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  6 16 as follows:
  6 17    a.  Fifty=two percent shall be used to support initiatives
  6 18 involving the acquisition, protection, and development of
  6 19 parks, preserves, and open spaces, including multipurpose
  6 20 trails, restroom facilities, shelter houses, and picnic
  6 21 facilities, but excluding athletic fields, baseball or softball
  6 22 diamonds, tennis courts, golf courses, swimming pools, and
  6 23 other sport facilities.
  6 24    b.  Twenty percent shall be used to support the same
  6 25 initiatives listed in subsection 8.
  6 26    c.  Twenty percent shall be used to support soil and water
  6 27 enhancement programs, including but not limited to woodland
  6 28 protection and enhancement, wildlife habitat preservation and
  6 29 enhancement, protection of highly erodible soils, and clean
  6 30 water.
  6 31    d.  Five percent shall be used to support historical resource
  6 32 development programs.
  6 33    e.  Three percent shall be used for the development and
  6 34 implementation of integrated roadside vegetation plans.
  6 35    8.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7  1 to support the following initiatives:
  7  2    a.  The maintenance and improvement of parks, preserves,
  7  3 wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native prairies, and
  7  4 wetlands.
  7  5    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  7  6    c.  Recreational purposes.
  7  7    d.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  7  8    e.  Education and outreach programs and projects that provide
  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 14 to support initiatives related to the design, establishment,
  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.

  6  9 and prioritization efforts, including as provided in chapter
  6 10 466B.
  6 11    b.  Surface water protection projects and practices,
  6 12 including but not limited to the installation of permanent
  6 13 vegetation cover, filter strips, grass waterways, and riparian
  6 14 forest buffers; dredging; and bank stabilization.
  6 15    7.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  6 16 as follows:
  6 17    a.  Fifty=two percent shall be used to support initiatives
  6 18 involving the acquisition, protection, and development of
  6 19 parks, preserves, and open spaces, including multipurpose
  6 20 trails, restroom facilities, shelter houses, and picnic
  6 21 facilities, but excluding athletic fields, baseball or softball
  6 22 diamonds, tennis courts, golf courses, swimming pools, and
  6 23 other sport facilities.
  6 24    b.  Twenty percent shall be used to support the same
  6 25 initiatives listed in subsection 8.
  6 26    c.  Twenty percent shall be used to support soil and water
  6 27 enhancement programs, including but not limited to woodland
  6 28 protection and enhancement, wildlife habitat preservation and
  6 29 enhancement, protection of highly erodible soils, and clean
  6 30 water.
  6 31    d.  Five percent shall be used to support historical resource
  6 32 development programs.
  6 33    e.  Three percent shall be used for the development and
  6 34 implementation of integrated roadside vegetation plans.
  6 35    8.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7  1 to support the following initiatives:
  7  2    a.  The maintenance and improvement of parks, preserves,
  7  3 wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native prairies, and
  7  4 wetlands.
  7  5    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  7  6    c.  Recreational purposes.
  7  7    d.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  7  8    e.  Education and outreach programs and projects that provide
  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 14 to support initiatives related to the design, establishment,
  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.
  7 22                           EXPLANATION
  7 23 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  7 24 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  7 25    This bill provides for an increase in the maximum local
  7 26 option sales tax rate to fund local natural resources and
  7 27 outdoor recreation projects.
  7 28    BACKGROUND.  Under current law, counties may impose a sales
  7 29 tax at the local level upon a petition of the voters or motions
  7 30 of city councils or the board of supervisors and after an
  7 31 election at which a majority of those voting favors imposition.
  7 32 A majority vote is also required for a repeal or rate change,
  7 33 but the governing body on its own motion may repeal the sales
  7 34 tax under certain circumstances.  The local option sales tax
  7 35 rate may not exceed one percent.
  8  1 Local option tax revenues collected in a county are remitted
  8  2 to the department of revenue (department) and, except for
  8  3 certain revenues attributable to urban renewal projects,
  8  4 distributed back to the county and cities within the county
  8  5 using a statutory formula involving population and historical
  8  6 property tax revenues.
  8  7    BILL CHANGES.  The bill increases the maximum local option
  8  8 sales tax rate that may be imposed by a county to one and
  8  9 three=eighths percent (1.375 percent) from one percent.  If a
  8 10 county votes to initially impose or to increase the tax rate
  8 11 above one percent, the bill requires tax revenues collected
  8 12 on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one percent to be
  8 13 remitted to counties and cities using the existing statutory
  8 14 formula, and then deposited in a special fund of the city or
  8 15 county and used exclusively for funding natural resources and
  8 16 outdoor recreation projects as described in the bill.
  8 17    The special fund moneys shall only be used to support
  8 18 voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for regulatory
  8 19 efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.  The bill allows
  8 20 for two or more cities or counties to enter into an agreement
  8 21 under Code chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  8 22 out any authorized initiative, and allows a city or county to
  8 23 deposit other local sales and services tax revenues it receives
  8 24 in its special natural resources and outdoor recreation fund.
  8 25    The bill also amends the calculation for determining
  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.
       LSB 5556YH (3) 86
       mm/sc
  5  6 local sales and services tax revenues received by it pursuant
  5  7 to the distribution formula in section 423B.7, subsections 3,
  5  8 4, and 5.
  5  9    3.  Two or more cities or counties may enter into an
  5 10 agreement under chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  5 11 out any initiative described in this section.
  5 12    4.  Twenty=three percent of the moneys in each fund shall be
  5 13 used to support the following initiatives:
  5 14    a.  The establishment, restoration, or enhancement of parks,
  5 15 preserves, forests, wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native
  5 16 prairies, and wetlands.
  5 17    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  5 18    c.  Recreational purposes.
  5 19    d.  Technical assistance and financial incentives to private
  5 20 landowners to promote the management of forests, fisheries,
  5 21 wetlands, and wildlife.
  5 22    e.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  5 23    f.  Education and outreach that provide instruction regarding
  5 24 natural history and the outdoors. The subjects of such
  5 25 instruction may relate to opportunities involving recreational
  5 26 purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  5 27    5.  Twenty percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  5 28 to support the following initiatives:
  5 29    a.  Soil conservation and watershed protection.
  5 30    b.  The conservation of highly erodible land.
  5 31    c.  Soil conservation or crop management practices used on
  5 32 land producing biomass for biorefineries, including cellulosic
  5 33 ethanol production.
  5 34    6.  Fourteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  5 35 to support the following initiatives:
  6  1    a.  Water resource projects to preserve watersheds, including
  6  2 but not limited to all of the following:
  6  3    (1)  Projects to protect, restore, or enhance water
  6  4 quality through the provision of financial assistance for
  6  5 impairment=based, locally directed watershed projects,
  6  6 including water resource restoration projects as defined in
  6  7 section 384.80.
  6  8    (2)  Regional and community watershed assessment, planning,
  6  9 and prioritization efforts, including as provided in chapter
  6 10 466B.
  6 11    b.  Surface water protection projects and practices,
  6 12 including but not limited to the installation of permanent
  6 13 vegetation cover, filter strips, grass waterways, and riparian
  6 14 forest buffers; dredging; and bank stabilization.
  6 15    7.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  6 16 as follows:
  6 17    a.  Fifty=two percent shall be used to support initiatives
  6 18 involving the acquisition, protection, and development of
  6 19 parks, preserves, and open spaces, including multipurpose
  6 20 trails, restroom facilities, shelter houses, and picnic
  6 21 facilities, but excluding athletic fields, baseball or softball
  6 22 diamonds, tennis courts, golf courses, swimming pools, and
  6 23 other sport facilities.
  6 24    b.  Twenty percent shall be used to support the same
  6 25 initiatives listed in subsection 8.
  6 26    c.  Twenty percent shall be used to support soil and water
  6 27 enhancement programs, including but not limited to woodland
  6 28 protection and enhancement, wildlife habitat preservation and
  6 29 enhancement, protection of highly erodible soils, and clean
  6 30 water.
  6 31    d.  Five percent shall be used to support historical resource
  6 32 development programs.
  6 33    e.  Three percent shall be used for the development and
  6 34 implementation of integrated roadside vegetation plans.
  6 35    8.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7  1 to support the following initiatives:
  7  2    a.  The maintenance and improvement of parks, preserves,
  7  3 wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native prairies, and
  7  4 wetlands.
  7  5    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  7  6    c.  Recreational purposes.
  7  7    d.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  7  8    e.  Education and outreach programs and projects that provide
  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 14 to support initiatives related to the design, establishment,
  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.

  6 15    7.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  6 16 as follows:
  6 17    a.  Fifty=two percent shall be used to support initiatives
  6 18 involving the acquisition, protection, and development of
  6 19 parks, preserves, and open spaces, including multipurpose
  6 20 trails, restroom facilities, shelter houses, and picnic
  6 21 facilities, but excluding athletic fields, baseball or softball
  6 22 diamonds, tennis courts, golf courses, swimming pools, and
  6 23 other sport facilities.
  6 24    b.  Twenty percent shall be used to support the same
  6 25 initiatives listed in subsection 8.
  6 26    c.  Twenty percent shall be used to support soil and water
  6 27 enhancement programs, including but not limited to woodland
  6 28 protection and enhancement, wildlife habitat preservation and
  6 29 enhancement, protection of highly erodible soils, and clean
  6 30 water.
  6 31    d.  Five percent shall be used to support historical resource
  6 32 development programs.
  6 33    e.  Three percent shall be used for the development and
  6 34 implementation of integrated roadside vegetation plans.
  6 35    8.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7  1 to support the following initiatives:
  7  2    a.  The maintenance and improvement of parks, preserves,
  7  3 wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native prairies, and
  7  4 wetlands.
  7  5    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  7  6    c.  Recreational purposes.
  7  7    d.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  7  8    e.  Education and outreach programs and projects that provide
  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 14 to support initiatives related to the design, establishment,
  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.
  7 22                           EXPLANATION
  7 23 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  7 24 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  7 25    This bill provides for an increase in the maximum local
  7 26 option sales tax rate to fund local natural resources and
  7 27 outdoor recreation projects.
  7 28    BACKGROUND.  Under current law, counties may impose a sales
  7 29 tax at the local level upon a petition of the voters or motions
  7 30 of city councils or the board of supervisors and after an
  7 31 election at which a majority of those voting favors imposition.
  7 32 A majority vote is also required for a repeal or rate change,
  7 33 but the governing body on its own motion may repeal the sales
  7 34 tax under certain circumstances.  The local option sales tax
  7 35 rate may not exceed one percent.
  8  1 Local option tax revenues collected in a county are remitted
  8  2 to the department of revenue (department) and, except for
  8  3 certain revenues attributable to urban renewal projects,
  8  4 distributed back to the county and cities within the county
  8  5 using a statutory formula involving population and historical
  8  6 property tax revenues.
  8  7    BILL CHANGES.  The bill increases the maximum local option
  8  8 sales tax rate that may be imposed by a county to one and
  8  9 three=eighths percent (1.375 percent) from one percent.  If a
  8 10 county votes to initially impose or to increase the tax rate
  8 11 above one percent, the bill requires tax revenues collected
  8 12 on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one percent to be
  8 13 remitted to counties and cities using the existing statutory
  8 14 formula, and then deposited in a special fund of the city or
  8 15 county and used exclusively for funding natural resources and
  8 16 outdoor recreation projects as described in the bill.
  8 17    The special fund moneys shall only be used to support
  8 18 voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for regulatory
  8 19 efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.  The bill allows
  8 20 for two or more cities or counties to enter into an agreement
  8 21 under Code chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  8 22 out any authorized initiative, and allows a city or county to
  8 23 deposit other local sales and services tax revenues it receives
  8 24 in its special natural resources and outdoor recreation fund.
  8 25    The bill also amends the calculation for determining
  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.
       LSB 5556YH (3) 86
       mm/sc
  5 10 agreement under chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  5 11 out any initiative described in this section.
  5 12    4.  Twenty=three percent of the moneys in each fund shall be
  5 13 used to support the following initiatives:
  5 14    a.  The establishment, restoration, or enhancement of parks,
  5 15 preserves, forests, wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native
  5 16 prairies, and wetlands.
  5 17    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  5 18    c.  Recreational purposes.
  5 19    d.  Technical assistance and financial incentives to private
  5 20 landowners to promote the management of forests, fisheries,
  5 21 wetlands, and wildlife.
  5 22    e.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  5 23    f.  Education and outreach that provide instruction regarding
  5 24 natural history and the outdoors. The subjects of such
  5 25 instruction may relate to opportunities involving recreational
  5 26 purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  5 27    5.  Twenty percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  5 28 to support the following initiatives:
  5 29    a.  Soil conservation and watershed protection.
  5 30    b.  The conservation of highly erodible land.
  5 31    c.  Soil conservation or crop management practices used on
  5 32 land producing biomass for biorefineries, including cellulosic
  5 33 ethanol production.
  5 34    6.  Fourteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  5 35 to support the following initiatives:
  6  1    a.  Water resource projects to preserve watersheds, including
  6  2 but not limited to all of the following:
  6  3    (1)  Projects to protect, restore, or enhance water
  6  4 quality through the provision of financial assistance for
  6  5 impairment=based, locally directed watershed projects,
  6  6 including water resource restoration projects as defined in
  6  7 section 384.80.
  6  8    (2)  Regional and community watershed assessment, planning,
  6  9 and prioritization efforts, including as provided in chapter
  6 10 466B.
  6 11    b.  Surface water protection projects and practices,
  6 12 including but not limited to the installation of permanent
  6 13 vegetation cover, filter strips, grass waterways, and riparian
  6 14 forest buffers; dredging; and bank stabilization.
  6 15    7.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  6 16 as follows:
  6 17    a.  Fifty=two percent shall be used to support initiatives
  6 18 involving the acquisition, protection, and development of
  6 19 parks, preserves, and open spaces, including multipurpose
  6 20 trails, restroom facilities, shelter houses, and picnic
  6 21 facilities, but excluding athletic fields, baseball or softball
  6 22 diamonds, tennis courts, golf courses, swimming pools, and
  6 23 other sport facilities.
  6 24    b.  Twenty percent shall be used to support the same
  6 25 initiatives listed in subsection 8.
  6 26    c.  Twenty percent shall be used to support soil and water
  6 27 enhancement programs, including but not limited to woodland
  6 28 protection and enhancement, wildlife habitat preservation and
  6 29 enhancement, protection of highly erodible soils, and clean
  6 30 water.
  6 31    d.  Five percent shall be used to support historical resource

  6 33    e.  Three percent shall be used for the development and

  6 35    8.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7  1 to support the following initiatives:
  7  2    a.  The maintenance and improvement of parks, preserves,

  7  5    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  7  6    c.  Recreational purposes.
  7  7    d.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  7  8    e.  Education and outreach programs and projects that provide
  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 14 to support initiatives related to the design, establishment,
  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.
  7 22                           EXPLANATION
  7 23 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  7 24 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  7 25    This bill provides for an increase in the maximum local
  7 26 option sales tax rate to fund local natural resources and
  7 27 outdoor recreation projects.
  7 28    BACKGROUND.  Under current law, counties may impose a sales
  7 29 tax at the local level upon a petition of the voters or motions
  7 30 of city councils or the board of supervisors and after an
  7 31 election at which a majority of those voting favors imposition.
  7 32 A majority vote is also required for a repeal or rate change,
  7 33 but the governing body on its own motion may repeal the sales
  7 34 tax under certain circumstances.  The local option sales tax
  7 35 rate may not exceed one percent.
  8  1 Local option tax revenues collected in a county are remitted
  8  2 to the department of revenue (department) and, except for
  8  3 certain revenues attributable to urban renewal projects,
  8  4 distributed back to the county and cities within the county
  8  5 using a statutory formula involving population and historical
  8  6 property tax revenues.
  8  7    BILL CHANGES.  The bill increases the maximum local option
  8  8 sales tax rate that may be imposed by a county to one and
  8  9 three=eighths percent (1.375 percent) from one percent.  If a
  8 10 county votes to initially impose or to increase the tax rate
  8 11 above one percent, the bill requires tax revenues collected
  8 12 on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one percent to be
  8 13 remitted to counties and cities using the existing statutory
  8 14 formula, and then deposited in a special fund of the city or
  8 15 county and used exclusively for funding natural resources and
  8 16 outdoor recreation projects as described in the bill.
  8 17    The special fund moneys shall only be used to support
  8 18 voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for regulatory
  8 19 efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.  The bill allows
  8 20 for two or more cities or counties to enter into an agreement
  8 21 under Code chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  8 22 out any authorized initiative, and allows a city or county to
  8 23 deposit other local sales and services tax revenues it receives
  8 24 in its special natural resources and outdoor recreation fund.
  8 25    The bill also amends the calculation for determining
  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.
       LSB 5556YH (3) 86
       mm/sc
  5 14    a.  The establishment, restoration, or enhancement of parks,
  5 15 preserves, forests, wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native
  5 16 prairies, and wetlands.
  5 17    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  5 18    c.  Recreational purposes.
  5 19    d.  Technical assistance and financial incentives to private
  5 20 landowners to promote the management of forests, fisheries,
  5 21 wetlands, and wildlife.
  5 22    e.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  5 23    f.  Education and outreach that provide instruction regarding
  5 24 natural history and the outdoors. The subjects of such
  5 25 instruction may relate to opportunities involving recreational
  5 26 purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  5 27    5.  Twenty percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  5 28 to support the following initiatives:
  5 29    a.  Soil conservation and watershed protection.
  5 30    b.  The conservation of highly erodible land.
  5 31    c.  Soil conservation or crop management practices used on
  5 32 land producing biomass for biorefineries, including cellulosic
  5 33 ethanol production.
  5 34    6.  Fourteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  5 35 to support the following initiatives:
  6  1    a.  Water resource projects to preserve watersheds, including
  6  2 but not limited to all of the following:
  6  3    (1)  Projects to protect, restore, or enhance water
  6  4 quality through the provision of financial assistance for
  6  5 impairment=based, locally directed watershed projects,
  6  6 including water resource restoration projects as defined in
  6  7 section 384.80.
  6  8    (2)  Regional and community watershed assessment, planning,
  6  9 and prioritization efforts, including as provided in chapter
  6 10 466B.
  6 11    b.  Surface water protection projects and practices,
  6 12 including but not limited to the installation of permanent
  6 13 vegetation cover, filter strips, grass waterways, and riparian
  6 14 forest buffers; dredging; and bank stabilization.
  6 15    7.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  6 16 as follows:
  6 17    a.  Fifty=two percent shall be used to support initiatives
  6 18 involving the acquisition, protection, and development of
  6 19 parks, preserves, and open spaces, including multipurpose
  6 20 trails, restroom facilities, shelter houses, and picnic
  6 21 facilities, but excluding athletic fields, baseball or softball
  6 22 diamonds, tennis courts, golf courses, swimming pools, and
  6 23 other sport facilities.
  6 24    b.  Twenty percent shall be used to support the same
  6 25 initiatives listed in subsection 8.
  6 26    c.  Twenty percent shall be used to support soil and water
  6 27 enhancement programs, including but not limited to woodland
  6 28 protection and enhancement, wildlife habitat preservation and
  6 29 enhancement, protection of highly erodible soils, and clean
  6 30 water.
  6 31    d.  Five percent shall be used to support historical resource
  6 32 development programs.
  6 33    e.  Three percent shall be used for the development and
  6 34 implementation of integrated roadside vegetation plans.
  6 35    8.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7  1 to support the following initiatives:
  7  2    a.  The maintenance and improvement of parks, preserves,
  7  3 wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native prairies, and
  7  4 wetlands.
  7  5    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  7  6    c.  Recreational purposes.
  7  7    d.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  7  8    e.  Education and outreach programs and projects that provide
  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 14 to support initiatives related to the design, establishment,
  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.

  8 11 above one percent, the bill requires tax revenues collected
  8 12 on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one percent to be
  8 13 remitted to counties and cities using the existing statutory
  8 14 formula, and then deposited in a special fund of the city or
  8 15 county and used exclusively for funding natural resources and
  8 16 outdoor recreation projects as described in the bill.
  8 17    The special fund moneys shall only be used to support
  8 18 voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for regulatory
  8 19 efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.  The bill allows
  8 20 for two or more cities or counties to enter into an agreement
  8 21 under Code chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  8 22 out any authorized initiative, and allows a city or county to
  8 23 deposit other local sales and services tax revenues it receives
  8 24 in its special natural resources and outdoor recreation fund.
  8 25    The bill also amends the calculation for determining
  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.
       LSB 5556YH (3) 86
       mm/sc
  5 18    c.  Recreational purposes.
  5 19    d.  Technical assistance and financial incentives to private
  5 20 landowners to promote the management of forests, fisheries,
  5 21 wetlands, and wildlife.
  5 22    e.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  5 23    f.  Education and outreach that provide instruction regarding
  5 24 natural history and the outdoors. The subjects of such
  5 25 instruction may relate to opportunities involving recreational
  5 26 purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  5 27    5.  Twenty percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  5 28 to support the following initiatives:
  5 29    a.  Soil conservation and watershed protection.
  5 30    b.  The conservation of highly erodible land.
  5 31    c.  Soil conservation or crop management practices used on
  5 32 land producing biomass for biorefineries, including cellulosic
  5 33 ethanol production.
  5 34    6.  Fourteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  5 35 to support the following initiatives:
  6  1    a.  Water resource projects to preserve watersheds, including
  6  2 but not limited to all of the following:
  6  3    (1)  Projects to protect, restore, or enhance water
  6  4 quality through the provision of financial assistance for
  6  5 impairment=based, locally directed watershed projects,
  6  6 including water resource restoration projects as defined in
  6  7 section 384.80.
  6  8    (2)  Regional and community watershed assessment, planning,
  6  9 and prioritization efforts, including as provided in chapter
  6 10 466B.
  6 11    b.  Surface water protection projects and practices,
  6 12 including but not limited to the installation of permanent
  6 13 vegetation cover, filter strips, grass waterways, and riparian
  6 14 forest buffers; dredging; and bank stabilization.
  6 15    7.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  6 16 as follows:
  6 17    a.  Fifty=two percent shall be used to support initiatives
  6 18 involving the acquisition, protection, and development of
  6 19 parks, preserves, and open spaces, including multipurpose
  6 20 trails, restroom facilities, shelter houses, and picnic
  6 21 facilities, but excluding athletic fields, baseball or softball
  6 22 diamonds, tennis courts, golf courses, swimming pools, and
  6 23 other sport facilities.
  6 24    b.  Twenty percent shall be used to support the same
  6 25 initiatives listed in subsection 8.
  6 26    c.  Twenty percent shall be used to support soil and water
  6 27 enhancement programs, including but not limited to woodland
  6 28 protection and enhancement, wildlife habitat preservation and
  6 29 enhancement, protection of highly erodible soils, and clean
  6 30 water.
  6 31    d.  Five percent shall be used to support historical resource
  6 32 development programs.
  6 33    e.  Three percent shall be used for the development and
  6 34 implementation of integrated roadside vegetation plans.
  6 35    8.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7  1 to support the following initiatives:
  7  2    a.  The maintenance and improvement of parks, preserves,
  7  3 wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native prairies, and
  7  4 wetlands.
  7  5    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  7  6    c.  Recreational purposes.
  7  7    d.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  7  8    e.  Education and outreach programs and projects that provide
  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 14 to support initiatives related to the design, establishment,
  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.
  7 22                           EXPLANATION
  7 23 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  7 24 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  7 25    This bill provides for an increase in the maximum local
  7 26 option sales tax rate to fund local natural resources and
  7 27 outdoor recreation projects.
  7 28    BACKGROUND.  Under current law, counties may impose a sales
  7 29 tax at the local level upon a petition of the voters or motions
  7 30 of city councils or the board of supervisors and after an
  7 31 election at which a majority of those voting favors imposition.
  7 32 A majority vote is also required for a repeal or rate change,
  7 33 but the governing body on its own motion may repeal the sales
  7 34 tax under certain circumstances.  The local option sales tax
  7 35 rate may not exceed one percent.
  8  1 Local option tax revenues collected in a county are remitted
  8  2 to the department of revenue (department) and, except for
  8  3 certain revenues attributable to urban renewal projects,
  8  4 distributed back to the county and cities within the county
  8  5 using a statutory formula involving population and historical
  8  6 property tax revenues.
  8  7    BILL CHANGES.  The bill increases the maximum local option
  8  8 sales tax rate that may be imposed by a county to one and
  8  9 three=eighths percent (1.375 percent) from one percent.  If a
  8 10 county votes to initially impose or to increase the tax rate
  8 11 above one percent, the bill requires tax revenues collected
  8 12 on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one percent to be
  8 13 remitted to counties and cities using the existing statutory
  8 14 formula, and then deposited in a special fund of the city or
  8 15 county and used exclusively for funding natural resources and
  8 16 outdoor recreation projects as described in the bill.
  8 17    The special fund moneys shall only be used to support
  8 18 voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for regulatory
  8 19 efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.  The bill allows
  8 20 for two or more cities or counties to enter into an agreement
  8 21 under Code chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  8 22 out any authorized initiative, and allows a city or county to
  8 23 deposit other local sales and services tax revenues it receives
  8 24 in its special natural resources and outdoor recreation fund.
  8 25    The bill also amends the calculation for determining
  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.
       LSB 5556YH (3) 86
       mm/sc

  6 22 diamonds, tennis courts, golf courses, swimming pools, and
  6 23 other sport facilities.
  6 24    b.  Twenty percent shall be used to support the same
  6 25 initiatives listed in subsection 8.
  6 26    c.  Twenty percent shall be used to support soil and water
  6 27 enhancement programs, including but not limited to woodland
  6 28 protection and enhancement, wildlife habitat preservation and
  6 29 enhancement, protection of highly erodible soils, and clean
  6 30 water.
  6 31    d.  Five percent shall be used to support historical resource
  6 32 development programs.
  6 33    e.  Three percent shall be used for the development and
  6 34 implementation of integrated roadside vegetation plans.
  6 35    8.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7  1 to support the following initiatives:
  7  2    a.  The maintenance and improvement of parks, preserves,
  7  3 wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native prairies, and
  7  4 wetlands.
  7  5    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  7  6    c.  Recreational purposes.
  7  7    d.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  7  8    e.  Education and outreach programs and projects that provide
  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 14 to support initiatives related to the design, establishment,
  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.
  7 22                           EXPLANATION
  7 23 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  7 24 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  7 25    This bill provides for an increase in the maximum local
  7 26 option sales tax rate to fund local natural resources and
  7 27 outdoor recreation projects.
  7 28    BACKGROUND.  Under current law, counties may impose a sales
  7 29 tax at the local level upon a petition of the voters or motions
  7 30 of city councils or the board of supervisors and after an
  7 31 election at which a majority of those voting favors imposition.
  7 32 A majority vote is also required for a repeal or rate change,
  7 33 but the governing body on its own motion may repeal the sales
  7 34 tax under certain circumstances.  The local option sales tax
  7 35 rate may not exceed one percent.
  8  1 Local option tax revenues collected in a county are remitted
  8  2 to the department of revenue (department) and, except for
  8  3 certain revenues attributable to urban renewal projects,
  8  4 distributed back to the county and cities within the county
  8  5 using a statutory formula involving population and historical
  8  6 property tax revenues.
  8  7    BILL CHANGES.  The bill increases the maximum local option
  8  8 sales tax rate that may be imposed by a county to one and
  8  9 three=eighths percent (1.375 percent) from one percent.  If a
  8 10 county votes to initially impose or to increase the tax rate
  8 11 above one percent, the bill requires tax revenues collected
  8 12 on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one percent to be
  8 13 remitted to counties and cities using the existing statutory
  8 14 formula, and then deposited in a special fund of the city or
  8 15 county and used exclusively for funding natural resources and
  8 16 outdoor recreation projects as described in the bill.
  8 17    The special fund moneys shall only be used to support
  8 18 voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for regulatory
  8 19 efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.  The bill allows
  8 20 for two or more cities or counties to enter into an agreement
  8 21 under Code chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  8 22 out any authorized initiative, and allows a city or county to
  8 23 deposit other local sales and services tax revenues it receives
  8 24 in its special natural resources and outdoor recreation fund.
  8 25    The bill also amends the calculation for determining
  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.
       LSB 5556YH (3) 86
       mm/sc
  5 23    f.  Education and outreach that provide instruction regarding
  5 24 natural history and the outdoors. The subjects of such
  5 25 instruction may relate to opportunities involving recreational
  5 26 purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  5 27    5.  Twenty percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  5 28 to support the following initiatives:
  5 29    a.  Soil conservation and watershed protection.
  5 30    b.  The conservation of highly erodible land.
  5 31    c.  Soil conservation or crop management practices used on
  5 32 land producing biomass for biorefineries, including cellulosic
  5 33 ethanol production.
  5 34    6.  Fourteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  5 35 to support the following initiatives:
  6  1    a.  Water resource projects to preserve watersheds, including
  6  2 but not limited to all of the following:
  6  3    (1)  Projects to protect, restore, or enhance water
  6  4 quality through the provision of financial assistance for
  6  5 impairment=based, locally directed watershed projects,
  6  6 including water resource restoration projects as defined in
  6  7 section 384.80.
  6  8    (2)  Regional and community watershed assessment, planning,
  6  9 and prioritization efforts, including as provided in chapter
  6 10 466B.
  6 11    b.  Surface water protection projects and practices,
  6 12 including but not limited to the installation of permanent
  6 13 vegetation cover, filter strips, grass waterways, and riparian
  6 14 forest buffers; dredging; and bank stabilization.
  6 15    7.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  6 16 as follows:
  6 17    a.  Fifty=two percent shall be used to support initiatives
  6 18 involving the acquisition, protection, and development of
  6 19 parks, preserves, and open spaces, including multipurpose
  6 20 trails, restroom facilities, shelter houses, and picnic
  6 21 facilities, but excluding athletic fields, baseball or softball
  6 22 diamonds, tennis courts, golf courses, swimming pools, and
  6 23 other sport facilities.
  6 24    b.  Twenty percent shall be used to support the same
  6 25 initiatives listed in subsection 8.
  6 26    c.  Twenty percent shall be used to support soil and water
  6 27 enhancement programs, including but not limited to woodland
  6 28 protection and enhancement, wildlife habitat preservation and
  6 29 enhancement, protection of highly erodible soils, and clean
  6 30 water.
  6 31    d.  Five percent shall be used to support historical resource
  6 32 development programs.
  6 33    e.  Three percent shall be used for the development and
  6 34 implementation of integrated roadside vegetation plans.
  6 35    8.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7  1 to support the following initiatives:
  7  2    a.  The maintenance and improvement of parks, preserves,
  7  3 wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native prairies, and
  7  4 wetlands.
  7  5    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  7  6    c.  Recreational purposes.
  7  7    d.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  7  8    e.  Education and outreach programs and projects that provide
  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 14 to support initiatives related to the design, establishment,
  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.

  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.
       LSB 5556YH (3) 86
       mm/sc
  5 27    5.  Twenty percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  5 28 to support the following initiatives:
  5 29    a.  Soil conservation and watershed protection.
  5 30    b.  The conservation of highly erodible land.
  5 31    c.  Soil conservation or crop management practices used on
  5 32 land producing biomass for biorefineries, including cellulosic
  5 33 ethanol production.
  5 34    6.  Fourteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  5 35 to support the following initiatives:
  6  1    a.  Water resource projects to preserve watersheds, including
  6  2 but not limited to all of the following:
  6  3    (1)  Projects to protect, restore, or enhance water
  6  4 quality through the provision of financial assistance for
  6  5 impairment=based, locally directed watershed projects,
  6  6 including water resource restoration projects as defined in
  6  7 section 384.80.
  6  8    (2)  Regional and community watershed assessment, planning,
  6  9 and prioritization efforts, including as provided in chapter
  6 10 466B.
  6 11    b.  Surface water protection projects and practices,
  6 12 including but not limited to the installation of permanent
  6 13 vegetation cover, filter strips, grass waterways, and riparian
  6 14 forest buffers; dredging; and bank stabilization.
  6 15    7.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  6 16 as follows:
  6 17    a.  Fifty=two percent shall be used to support initiatives
  6 18 involving the acquisition, protection, and development of
  6 19 parks, preserves, and open spaces, including multipurpose
  6 20 trails, restroom facilities, shelter houses, and picnic
  6 21 facilities, but excluding athletic fields, baseball or softball
  6 22 diamonds, tennis courts, golf courses, swimming pools, and
  6 23 other sport facilities.
  6 24    b.  Twenty percent shall be used to support the same
  6 25 initiatives listed in subsection 8.
  6 26    c.  Twenty percent shall be used to support soil and water
  6 27 enhancement programs, including but not limited to woodland
  6 28 protection and enhancement, wildlife habitat preservation and
  6 29 enhancement, protection of highly erodible soils, and clean
  6 30 water.
  6 31    d.  Five percent shall be used to support historical resource
  6 32 development programs.
  6 33    e.  Three percent shall be used for the development and
  6 34 implementation of integrated roadside vegetation plans.
  6 35    8.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7  1 to support the following initiatives:
  7  2    a.  The maintenance and improvement of parks, preserves,
  7  3 wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native prairies, and
  7  4 wetlands.
  7  5    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  7  6    c.  Recreational purposes.
  7  7    d.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  7  8    e.  Education and outreach programs and projects that provide
  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 14 to support initiatives related to the design, establishment,
  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.
  7 22                           EXPLANATION
  7 23 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  7 24 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  7 25    This bill provides for an increase in the maximum local
  7 26 option sales tax rate to fund local natural resources and
  7 27 outdoor recreation projects.
  7 28    BACKGROUND.  Under current law, counties may impose a sales
  7 29 tax at the local level upon a petition of the voters or motions
  7 30 of city councils or the board of supervisors and after an
  7 31 election at which a majority of those voting favors imposition.
  7 32 A majority vote is also required for a repeal or rate change,
  7 33 but the governing body on its own motion may repeal the sales
  7 34 tax under certain circumstances.  The local option sales tax
  7 35 rate may not exceed one percent.
  8  1 Local option tax revenues collected in a county are remitted
  8  2 to the department of revenue (department) and, except for
  8  3 certain revenues attributable to urban renewal projects,
  8  4 distributed back to the county and cities within the county
  8  5 using a statutory formula involving population and historical
  8  6 property tax revenues.
  8  7    BILL CHANGES.  The bill increases the maximum local option
  8  8 sales tax rate that may be imposed by a county to one and
  8  9 three=eighths percent (1.375 percent) from one percent.  If a
  8 10 county votes to initially impose or to increase the tax rate
  8 11 above one percent, the bill requires tax revenues collected
  8 12 on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one percent to be
  8 13 remitted to counties and cities using the existing statutory
  8 14 formula, and then deposited in a special fund of the city or
  8 15 county and used exclusively for funding natural resources and
  8 16 outdoor recreation projects as described in the bill.
  8 17    The special fund moneys shall only be used to support
  8 18 voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for regulatory
  8 19 efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.  The bill allows
  8 20 for two or more cities or counties to enter into an agreement
  8 21 under Code chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  8 22 out any authorized initiative, and allows a city or county to
  8 23 deposit other local sales and services tax revenues it receives
  8 24 in its special natural resources and outdoor recreation fund.
  8 25    The bill also amends the calculation for determining
  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.
       LSB 5556YH (3) 86
       mm/sc
  5 28 to support the following initiatives:
  5 29    a.  Soil conservation and watershed protection.
  5 30    b.  The conservation of highly erodible land.
  5 31    c.  Soil conservation or crop management practices used on
  5 32 land producing biomass for biorefineries, including cellulosic
  5 33 ethanol production.
  5 34    6.  Fourteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  5 35 to support the following initiatives:
  6  1    a.  Water resource projects to preserve watersheds, including
  6  2 but not limited to all of the following:
  6  3    (1)  Projects to protect, restore, or enhance water

  6  8    (2)  Regional and community watershed assessment, planning,
  6  9 and prioritization efforts, including as provided in chapter
  6 10 466B.
