  8 14 formula, and then deposited in a special fund of the city or
  8 15 county and used exclusively for funding natural resources and
  8 16 outdoor recreation projects as described in the bill.
  8 17    The special fund moneys shall only be used to support
  8 18 voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for regulatory
  8 19 efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.  The bill allows
  8 20 for two or more cities or counties to enter into an agreement
  8 21 under Code chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  8 22 out any authorized initiative, and allows a city or county to
  8 23 deposit other local sales and services tax revenues it receives
  8 24 in its special natural resources and outdoor recreation fund.
  8 25    The bill also amends the calculation for determining
  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.
       LSB 5556YH (3) 86
       mm/sc
  5 32 land producing biomass for biorefineries, including cellulosic
  5 33 ethanol production.
  5 34    6.  Fourteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  5 35 to support the following initiatives:
  6  1    a.  Water resource projects to preserve watersheds, including
  6  2 but not limited to all of the following:
  6  3    (1)  Projects to protect, restore, or enhance water
  6  4 quality through the provision of financial assistance for
  6  5 impairment=based, locally directed watershed projects,
  6  6 including water resource restoration projects as defined in
  6  7 section 384.80.
  6  8    (2)  Regional and community watershed assessment, planning,
  6  9 and prioritization efforts, including as provided in chapter
  6 10 466B.
  6 11    b.  Surface water protection projects and practices,
  6 12 including but not limited to the installation of permanent
  6 13 vegetation cover, filter strips, grass waterways, and riparian
  6 14 forest buffers; dredging; and bank stabilization.
  6 15    7.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  6 16 as follows:
  6 17    a.  Fifty=two percent shall be used to support initiatives
  6 18 involving the acquisition, protection, and development of
  6 19 parks, preserves, and open spaces, including multipurpose
  6 20 trails, restroom facilities, shelter houses, and picnic
  6 21 facilities, but excluding athletic fields, baseball or softball
  6 22 diamonds, tennis courts, golf courses, swimming pools, and
  6 23 other sport facilities.
  6 24    b.  Twenty percent shall be used to support the same
  6 25 initiatives listed in subsection 8.
  6 26    c.  Twenty percent shall be used to support soil and water
  6 27 enhancement programs, including but not limited to woodland
  6 28 protection and enhancement, wildlife habitat preservation and
  6 29 enhancement, protection of highly erodible soils, and clean
  6 30 water.
  6 31    d.  Five percent shall be used to support historical resource
  6 32 development programs.
  6 33    e.  Three percent shall be used for the development and
  6 34 implementation of integrated roadside vegetation plans.
  6 35    8.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7  1 to support the following initiatives:
  7  2    a.  The maintenance and improvement of parks, preserves,
  7  3 wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native prairies, and
  7  4 wetlands.
  7  5    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  7  6    c.  Recreational purposes.
  7  7    d.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  7  8    e.  Education and outreach programs and projects that provide
  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 14 to support initiatives related to the design, establishment,
  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.
  7 22                           EXPLANATION
  7 23 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  7 24 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  7 25    This bill provides for an increase in the maximum local
  7 26 option sales tax rate to fund local natural resources and
  7 27 outdoor recreation projects.
  7 28    BACKGROUND.  Under current law, counties may impose a sales
  7 29 tax at the local level upon a petition of the voters or motions
  7 30 of city councils or the board of supervisors and after an
  7 31 election at which a majority of those voting favors imposition.
  7 32 A majority vote is also required for a repeal or rate change,
  7 33 but the governing body on its own motion may repeal the sales
  7 34 tax under certain circumstances.  The local option sales tax
  7 35 rate may not exceed one percent.
  8  1 Local option tax revenues collected in a county are remitted
  8  2 to the department of revenue (department) and, except for
  8  3 certain revenues attributable to urban renewal projects,
  8  4 distributed back to the county and cities within the county
  8  5 using a statutory formula involving population and historical
  8  6 property tax revenues.
  8  7    BILL CHANGES.  The bill increases the maximum local option
  8  8 sales tax rate that may be imposed by a county to one and
  8  9 three=eighths percent (1.375 percent) from one percent.  If a
  8 10 county votes to initially impose or to increase the tax rate
  8 11 above one percent, the bill requires tax revenues collected
  8 12 on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one percent to be
  8 13 remitted to counties and cities using the existing statutory
  8 14 formula, and then deposited in a special fund of the city or
  8 15 county and used exclusively for funding natural resources and
  8 16 outdoor recreation projects as described in the bill.
  8 17    The special fund moneys shall only be used to support
  8 18 voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for regulatory
  8 19 efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.  The bill allows
  8 20 for two or more cities or counties to enter into an agreement
  8 21 under Code chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  8 22 out any authorized initiative, and allows a city or county to
  8 23 deposit other local sales and services tax revenues it receives
  8 24 in its special natural resources and outdoor recreation fund.
  8 25    The bill also amends the calculation for determining
  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.
       LSB 5556YH (3) 86
       mm/sc
  5 33 ethanol production.
  5 34    6.  Fourteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  5 35 to support the following initiatives:
  6  1    a.  Water resource projects to preserve watersheds, including
  6  2 but not limited to all of the following:
  6  3    (1)  Projects to protect, restore, or enhance water
  6  4 quality through the provision of financial assistance for
  6  5 impairment=based, locally directed watershed projects,
  6  6 including water resource restoration projects as defined in
  6  7 section 384.80.
  6  8    (2)  Regional and community watershed assessment, planning,
  6  9 and prioritization efforts, including as provided in chapter
  6 10 466B.
  6 11    b.  Surface water protection projects and practices,
  6 12 including but not limited to the installation of permanent
  6 13 vegetation cover, filter strips, grass waterways, and riparian
  6 14 forest buffers; dredging; and bank stabilization.
  6 15    7.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used

  6 24    b.  Twenty percent shall be used to support the same

  6 26    c.  Twenty percent shall be used to support soil and water

  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.

  7 16 water trails.

  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.
       LSB 5556YH (3) 86
       mm/sc
  6  2 but not limited to all of the following:
  6  3    (1)  Projects to protect, restore, or enhance water
  6  4 quality through the provision of financial assistance for
  6  5 impairment=based, locally directed watershed projects,
  6  6 including water resource restoration projects as defined in
  6  7 section 384.80.
  6  8    (2)  Regional and community watershed assessment, planning,
  6  9 and prioritization efforts, including as provided in chapter
  6 10 466B.
  6 11    b.  Surface water protection projects and practices,
  6 12 including but not limited to the installation of permanent
  6 13 vegetation cover, filter strips, grass waterways, and riparian
  6 14 forest buffers; dredging; and bank stabilization.
  6 15    7.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  6 16 as follows:
  6 17    a.  Fifty=two percent shall be used to support initiatives
  6 18 involving the acquisition, protection, and development of
  6 19 parks, preserves, and open spaces, including multipurpose
  6 20 trails, restroom facilities, shelter houses, and picnic
  6 21 facilities, but excluding athletic fields, baseball or softball
  6 22 diamonds, tennis courts, golf courses, swimming pools, and
  6 23 other sport facilities.
  6 24    b.  Twenty percent shall be used to support the same
  6 25 initiatives listed in subsection 8.
  6 26    c.  Twenty percent shall be used to support soil and water
  6 27 enhancement programs, including but not limited to woodland
  6 28 protection and enhancement, wildlife habitat preservation and
  6 29 enhancement, protection of highly erodible soils, and clean
  6 30 water.
  6 31    d.  Five percent shall be used to support historical resource
  6 32 development programs.
  6 33    e.  Three percent shall be used for the development and
  6 34 implementation of integrated roadside vegetation plans.
  6 35    8.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7  1 to support the following initiatives:
  7  2    a.  The maintenance and improvement of parks, preserves,
  7  3 wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native prairies, and
  7  4 wetlands.
  7  5    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  7  6    c.  Recreational purposes.
  7  7    d.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  7  8    e.  Education and outreach programs and projects that provide
  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 14 to support initiatives related to the design, establishment,
  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.
  7 22                           EXPLANATION
  7 23 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  7 24 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  7 25    This bill provides for an increase in the maximum local
  7 26 option sales tax rate to fund local natural resources and
  7 27 outdoor recreation projects.
  7 28    BACKGROUND.  Under current law, counties may impose a sales
  7 29 tax at the local level upon a petition of the voters or motions
  7 30 of city councils or the board of supervisors and after an
  7 31 election at which a majority of those voting favors imposition.
  7 32 A majority vote is also required for a repeal or rate change,
  7 33 but the governing body on its own motion may repeal the sales
  7 34 tax under certain circumstances.  The local option sales tax
  7 35 rate may not exceed one percent.
  8  1 Local option tax revenues collected in a county are remitted
  8  2 to the department of revenue (department) and, except for
  8  3 certain revenues attributable to urban renewal projects,
  8  4 distributed back to the county and cities within the county
  8  5 using a statutory formula involving population and historical
  8  6 property tax revenues.
  8  7    BILL CHANGES.  The bill increases the maximum local option
  8  8 sales tax rate that may be imposed by a county to one and
  8  9 three=eighths percent (1.375 percent) from one percent.  If a
  8 10 county votes to initially impose or to increase the tax rate
  8 11 above one percent, the bill requires tax revenues collected
  8 12 on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one percent to be
  8 13 remitted to counties and cities using the existing statutory
  8 14 formula, and then deposited in a special fund of the city or
  8 15 county and used exclusively for funding natural resources and
  8 16 outdoor recreation projects as described in the bill.
  8 17    The special fund moneys shall only be used to support
  8 18 voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for regulatory
  8 19 efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.  The bill allows
  8 20 for two or more cities or counties to enter into an agreement
  8 21 under Code chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  8 22 out any authorized initiative, and allows a city or county to
  8 23 deposit other local sales and services tax revenues it receives
  8 24 in its special natural resources and outdoor recreation fund.
  8 25    The bill also amends the calculation for determining
  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.
       LSB 5556YH (3) 86
       mm/sc
  6  3    (1)  Projects to protect, restore, or enhance water
  6  4 quality through the provision of financial assistance for
  6  5 impairment=based, locally directed watershed projects,
  6  6 including water resource restoration projects as defined in
  6  7 section 384.80.
  6  8    (2)  Regional and community watershed assessment, planning,
  6  9 and prioritization efforts, including as provided in chapter
  6 10 466B.
  6 11    b.  Surface water protection projects and practices,
  6 12 including but not limited to the installation of permanent

  7  7    d.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  7  8    e.  Education and outreach programs and projects that provide
  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 14 to support initiatives related to the design, establishment,
  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.
  7 22                           EXPLANATION
  7 23 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  7 24 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  7 25    This bill provides for an increase in the maximum local
  7 26 option sales tax rate to fund local natural resources and
  7 27 outdoor recreation projects.
  7 28    BACKGROUND.  Under current law, counties may impose a sales
  7 29 tax at the local level upon a petition of the voters or motions
  7 30 of city councils or the board of supervisors and after an
  7 31 election at which a majority of those voting favors imposition.
  7 32 A majority vote is also required for a repeal or rate change,
  7 33 but the governing body on its own motion may repeal the sales
  7 34 tax under certain circumstances.  The local option sales tax
  7 35 rate may not exceed one percent.
  8  1 Local option tax revenues collected in a county are remitted
  8  2 to the department of revenue (department) and, except for
  8  3 certain revenues attributable to urban renewal projects,
  8  4 distributed back to the county and cities within the county
  8  5 using a statutory formula involving population and historical
  8  6 property tax revenues.
  8  7    BILL CHANGES.  The bill increases the maximum local option
  8  8 sales tax rate that may be imposed by a county to one and
  8  9 three=eighths percent (1.375 percent) from one percent.  If a
  8 10 county votes to initially impose or to increase the tax rate
  8 11 above one percent, the bill requires tax revenues collected
  8 12 on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one percent to be
  8 13 remitted to counties and cities using the existing statutory
  8 14 formula, and then deposited in a special fund of the city or
  8 15 county and used exclusively for funding natural resources and
  8 16 outdoor recreation projects as described in the bill.
  8 17    The special fund moneys shall only be used to support
  8 18 voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for regulatory
  8 19 efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.  The bill allows
  8 20 for two or more cities or counties to enter into an agreement
  8 21 under Code chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  8 22 out any authorized initiative, and allows a city or county to
  8 23 deposit other local sales and services tax revenues it receives
  8 24 in its special natural resources and outdoor recreation fund.
  8 25    The bill also amends the calculation for determining
  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.
       LSB 5556YH (3) 86
       mm/sc
  6  8    (2)  Regional and community watershed assessment, planning,
  6  9 and prioritization efforts, including as provided in chapter
  6 10 466B.
  6 11    b.  Surface water protection projects and practices,
  6 12 including but not limited to the installation of permanent
  6 13 vegetation cover, filter strips, grass waterways, and riparian
  6 14 forest buffers; dredging; and bank stabilization.
  6 15    7.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  6 16 as follows:
  6 17    a.  Fifty=two percent shall be used to support initiatives
  6 18 involving the acquisition, protection, and development of
  6 19 parks, preserves, and open spaces, including multipurpose
  6 20 trails, restroom facilities, shelter houses, and picnic
  6 21 facilities, but excluding athletic fields, baseball or softball
  6 22 diamonds, tennis courts, golf courses, swimming pools, and
  6 23 other sport facilities.
  6 24    b.  Twenty percent shall be used to support the same
  6 25 initiatives listed in subsection 8.
  6 26    c.  Twenty percent shall be used to support soil and water
  6 27 enhancement programs, including but not limited to woodland
  6 28 protection and enhancement, wildlife habitat preservation and
  6 29 enhancement, protection of highly erodible soils, and clean
  6 30 water.
  6 31    d.  Five percent shall be used to support historical resource
  6 32 development programs.
  6 33    e.  Three percent shall be used for the development and
  6 34 implementation of integrated roadside vegetation plans.
  6 35    8.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7  1 to support the following initiatives:
  7  2    a.  The maintenance and improvement of parks, preserves,
  7  3 wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native prairies, and
  7  4 wetlands.
  7  5    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  7  6    c.  Recreational purposes.
  7  7    d.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  7  8    e.  Education and outreach programs and projects that provide
  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 14 to support initiatives related to the design, establishment,
  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.

  6 20 trails, restroom facilities, shelter houses, and picnic
  6 21 facilities, but excluding athletic fields, baseball or softball
  6 22 diamonds, tennis courts, golf courses, swimming pools, and
  6 23 other sport facilities.
  6 24    b.  Twenty percent shall be used to support the same
  6 25 initiatives listed in subsection 8.
  6 26    c.  Twenty percent shall be used to support soil and water
  6 27 enhancement programs, including but not limited to woodland
  6 28 protection and enhancement, wildlife habitat preservation and
  6 29 enhancement, protection of highly erodible soils, and clean
  6 30 water.
  6 31    d.  Five percent shall be used to support historical resource
  6 32 development programs.
  6 33    e.  Three percent shall be used for the development and
  6 34 implementation of integrated roadside vegetation plans.
  6 35    8.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7  1 to support the following initiatives:
  7  2    a.  The maintenance and improvement of parks, preserves,
  7  3 wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native prairies, and
  7  4 wetlands.
  7  5    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  7  6    c.  Recreational purposes.
  7  7    d.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  7  8    e.  Education and outreach programs and projects that provide
  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 14 to support initiatives related to the design, establishment,
  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.
  7 22                           EXPLANATION
  7 23 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  7 24 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  7 25    This bill provides for an increase in the maximum local
  7 26 option sales tax rate to fund local natural resources and
  7 27 outdoor recreation projects.
  7 28    BACKGROUND.  Under current law, counties may impose a sales
  7 29 tax at the local level upon a petition of the voters or motions
  7 30 of city councils or the board of supervisors and after an
  7 31 election at which a majority of those voting favors imposition.
  7 32 A majority vote is also required for a repeal or rate change,
  7 33 but the governing body on its own motion may repeal the sales
  7 34 tax under certain circumstances.  The local option sales tax
  7 35 rate may not exceed one percent.
  8  1 Local option tax revenues collected in a county are remitted
  8  2 to the department of revenue (department) and, except for
  8  3 certain revenues attributable to urban renewal projects,
  8  4 distributed back to the county and cities within the county
  8  5 using a statutory formula involving population and historical
  8  6 property tax revenues.
  8  7    BILL CHANGES.  The bill increases the maximum local option
  8  8 sales tax rate that may be imposed by a county to one and
  8  9 three=eighths percent (1.375 percent) from one percent.  If a
  8 10 county votes to initially impose or to increase the tax rate
  8 11 above one percent, the bill requires tax revenues collected
  8 12 on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one percent to be
  8 13 remitted to counties and cities using the existing statutory
  8 14 formula, and then deposited in a special fund of the city or
  8 15 county and used exclusively for funding natural resources and
  8 16 outdoor recreation projects as described in the bill.
  8 17    The special fund moneys shall only be used to support
  8 18 voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for regulatory
  8 19 efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.  The bill allows
  8 20 for two or more cities or counties to enter into an agreement
  8 21 under Code chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  8 22 out any authorized initiative, and allows a city or county to
  8 23 deposit other local sales and services tax revenues it receives
  8 24 in its special natural resources and outdoor recreation fund.
  8 25    The bill also amends the calculation for determining
  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.
       LSB 5556YH (3) 86
       mm/sc
  6 14 forest buffers; dredging; and bank stabilization.
  6 15    7.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  6 16 as follows:
  6 17    a.  Fifty=two percent shall be used to support initiatives
  6 18 involving the acquisition, protection, and development of
  6 19 parks, preserves, and open spaces, including multipurpose
  6 20 trails, restroom facilities, shelter houses, and picnic
  6 21 facilities, but excluding athletic fields, baseball or softball
  6 22 diamonds, tennis courts, golf courses, swimming pools, and
  6 23 other sport facilities.
  6 24    b.  Twenty percent shall be used to support the same
  6 25 initiatives listed in subsection 8.
  6 26    c.  Twenty percent shall be used to support soil and water
  6 27 enhancement programs, including but not limited to woodland
  6 28 protection and enhancement, wildlife habitat preservation and
  6 29 enhancement, protection of highly erodible soils, and clean
  6 30 water.
  6 31    d.  Five percent shall be used to support historical resource
  6 32 development programs.
  6 33    e.  Three percent shall be used for the development and
  6 34 implementation of integrated roadside vegetation plans.
  6 35    8.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used

  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.

  7  2    a.  The maintenance and improvement of parks, preserves,
  7  3 wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native prairies, and
  7  4 wetlands.
  7  5    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  7  6    c.  Recreational purposes.
  7  7    d.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  7  8    e.  Education and outreach programs and projects that provide
  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 14 to support initiatives related to the design, establishment,
  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.
  7 22                           EXPLANATION
  7 23 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  7 24 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  7 25    This bill provides for an increase in the maximum local
  7 26 option sales tax rate to fund local natural resources and
  7 27 outdoor recreation projects.
  7 28    BACKGROUND.  Under current law, counties may impose a sales
  7 29 tax at the local level upon a petition of the voters or motions
  7 30 of city councils or the board of supervisors and after an
  7 31 election at which a majority of those voting favors imposition.
  7 32 A majority vote is also required for a repeal or rate change,
  7 33 but the governing body on its own motion may repeal the sales
  7 34 tax under certain circumstances.  The local option sales tax
  7 35 rate may not exceed one percent.
  8  1 Local option tax revenues collected in a county are remitted
  8  2 to the department of revenue (department) and, except for
  8  3 certain revenues attributable to urban renewal projects,
  8  4 distributed back to the county and cities within the county
  8  5 using a statutory formula involving population and historical
  8  6 property tax revenues.
  8  7    BILL CHANGES.  The bill increases the maximum local option
  8  8 sales tax rate that may be imposed by a county to one and
  8  9 three=eighths percent (1.375 percent) from one percent.  If a
  8 10 county votes to initially impose or to increase the tax rate
  8 11 above one percent, the bill requires tax revenues collected
  8 12 on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one percent to be
  8 13 remitted to counties and cities using the existing statutory
  8 14 formula, and then deposited in a special fund of the city or
  8 15 county and used exclusively for funding natural resources and
  8 16 outdoor recreation projects as described in the bill.
  8 17    The special fund moneys shall only be used to support
  8 18 voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for regulatory
  8 19 efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.  The bill allows
  8 20 for two or more cities or counties to enter into an agreement
  8 21 under Code chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  8 22 out any authorized initiative, and allows a city or county to
  8 23 deposit other local sales and services tax revenues it receives
  8 24 in its special natural resources and outdoor recreation fund.
  8 25    The bill also amends the calculation for determining
  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.
       LSB 5556YH (3) 86
       mm/sc
  6 20 trails, restroom facilities, shelter houses, and picnic
  6 21 facilities, but excluding athletic fields, baseball or softball
  6 22 diamonds, tennis courts, golf courses, swimming pools, and
  6 23 other sport facilities.
  6 24    b.  Twenty percent shall be used to support the same
  6 25 initiatives listed in subsection 8.
  6 26    c.  Twenty percent shall be used to support soil and water
  6 27 enhancement programs, including but not limited to woodland
  6 28 protection and enhancement, wildlife habitat preservation and
  6 29 enhancement, protection of highly erodible soils, and clean
  6 30 water.
  6 31    d.  Five percent shall be used to support historical resource
  6 32 development programs.
  6 33    e.  Three percent shall be used for the development and
  6 34 implementation of integrated roadside vegetation plans.
  6 35    8.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7  1 to support the following initiatives:
  7  2    a.  The maintenance and improvement of parks, preserves,
  7  3 wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native prairies, and
  7  4 wetlands.
  7  5    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  7  6    c.  Recreational purposes.
  7  7    d.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  7  8    e.  Education and outreach programs and projects that provide
  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 14 to support initiatives related to the design, establishment,
  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.

  8 18 voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for regulatory
  8 19 efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.  The bill allows
  8 20 for two or more cities or counties to enter into an agreement
  8 21 under Code chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  8 22 out any authorized initiative, and allows a city or county to
  8 23 deposit other local sales and services tax revenues it receives
  8 24 in its special natural resources and outdoor recreation fund.
  8 25    The bill also amends the calculation for determining
  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.
       LSB 5556YH (3) 86
       mm/sc
  6 26    c.  Twenty percent shall be used to support soil and water
  6 27 enhancement programs, including but not limited to woodland
  6 28 protection and enhancement, wildlife habitat preservation and
  6 29 enhancement, protection of highly erodible soils, and clean
  6 30 water.
  6 31    d.  Five percent shall be used to support historical resource
  6 32 development programs.
  6 33    e.  Three percent shall be used for the development and
  6 34 implementation of integrated roadside vegetation plans.
  6 35    8.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7  1 to support the following initiatives:
  7  2    a.  The maintenance and improvement of parks, preserves,
  7  3 wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native prairies, and
  7  4 wetlands.
  7  5    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  7  6    c.  Recreational purposes.
  7  7    d.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  7  8    e.  Education and outreach programs and projects that provide
  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 14 to support initiatives related to the design, establishment,
  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.
  7 22                           EXPLANATION
  7 23 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  7 24 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  7 25    This bill provides for an increase in the maximum local
  7 26 option sales tax rate to fund local natural resources and
  7 27 outdoor recreation projects.
  7 28    BACKGROUND.  Under current law, counties may impose a sales
  7 29 tax at the local level upon a petition of the voters or motions
  7 30 of city councils or the board of supervisors and after an
  7 31 election at which a majority of those voting favors imposition.
  7 32 A majority vote is also required for a repeal or rate change,
  7 33 but the governing body on its own motion may repeal the sales
  7 34 tax under certain circumstances.  The local option sales tax
  7 35 rate may not exceed one percent.
  8  1 Local option tax revenues collected in a county are remitted
  8  2 to the department of revenue (department) and, except for
  8  3 certain revenues attributable to urban renewal projects,
  8  4 distributed back to the county and cities within the county
  8  5 using a statutory formula involving population and historical
  8  6 property tax revenues.
  8  7    BILL CHANGES.  The bill increases the maximum local option
  8  8 sales tax rate that may be imposed by a county to one and
  8  9 three=eighths percent (1.375 percent) from one percent.  If a
  8 10 county votes to initially impose or to increase the tax rate
  8 11 above one percent, the bill requires tax revenues collected
  8 12 on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one percent to be
  8 13 remitted to counties and cities using the existing statutory
  8 14 formula, and then deposited in a special fund of the city or
  8 15 county and used exclusively for funding natural resources and
  8 16 outdoor recreation projects as described in the bill.
  8 17    The special fund moneys shall only be used to support
  8 18 voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for regulatory
  8 19 efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.  The bill allows
  8 20 for two or more cities or counties to enter into an agreement
  8 21 under Code chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  8 22 out any authorized initiative, and allows a city or county to
  8 23 deposit other local sales and services tax revenues it receives
  8 24 in its special natural resources and outdoor recreation fund.
  8 25    The bill also amends the calculation for determining
  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.
       LSB 5556YH (3) 86
       mm/sc
  6 27 enhancement programs, including but not limited to woodland
  6 28 protection and enhancement, wildlife habitat preservation and
  6 29 enhancement, protection of highly erodible soils, and clean
  6 30 water.
  6 31    d.  Five percent shall be used to support historical resource
  6 32 development programs.
  6 33    e.  Three percent shall be used for the development and
  6 34 implementation of integrated roadside vegetation plans.
  6 35    8.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7  1 to support the following initiatives:
  7  2    a.  The maintenance and improvement of parks, preserves,
  7  3 wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native prairies, and
  7  4 wetlands.
  7  5    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  7  6    c.  Recreational purposes.
  7  7    d.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  7  8    e.  Education and outreach programs and projects that provide
  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used

  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.

  7  1 to support the following initiatives:
  7  2    a.  The maintenance and improvement of parks, preserves,
  7  3 wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native prairies, and
  7  4 wetlands.
  7  5    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  7  6    c.  Recreational purposes.
  7  7    d.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  7  8    e.  Education and outreach programs and projects that provide
  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 14 to support initiatives related to the design, establishment,
  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.
  7 22                           EXPLANATION
  7 23 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  7 24 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  7 25    This bill provides for an increase in the maximum local
  7 26 option sales tax rate to fund local natural resources and
  7 27 outdoor recreation projects.
  7 28    BACKGROUND.  Under current law, counties may impose a sales
  7 29 tax at the local level upon a petition of the voters or motions
  7 30 of city councils or the board of supervisors and after an
  7 31 election at which a majority of those voting favors imposition.
  7 32 A majority vote is also required for a repeal or rate change,
  7 33 but the governing body on its own motion may repeal the sales
  7 34 tax under certain circumstances.  The local option sales tax
  7 35 rate may not exceed one percent.
  8  1 Local option tax revenues collected in a county are remitted
  8  2 to the department of revenue (department) and, except for
  8  3 certain revenues attributable to urban renewal projects,
  8  4 distributed back to the county and cities within the county
  8  5 using a statutory formula involving population and historical
  8  6 property tax revenues.
  8  7    BILL CHANGES.  The bill increases the maximum local option
  8  8 sales tax rate that may be imposed by a county to one and
  8  9 three=eighths percent (1.375 percent) from one percent.  If a
  8 10 county votes to initially impose or to increase the tax rate
  8 11 above one percent, the bill requires tax revenues collected
  8 12 on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one percent to be
  8 13 remitted to counties and cities using the existing statutory
  8 14 formula, and then deposited in a special fund of the city or
  8 15 county and used exclusively for funding natural resources and
  8 16 outdoor recreation projects as described in the bill.
  8 17    The special fund moneys shall only be used to support
  8 18 voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for regulatory
  8 19 efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.  The bill allows
  8 20 for two or more cities or counties to enter into an agreement
  8 21 under Code chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  8 22 out any authorized initiative, and allows a city or county to
  8 23 deposit other local sales and services tax revenues it receives
  8 24 in its special natural resources and outdoor recreation fund.
  8 25    The bill also amends the calculation for determining
  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.
       LSB 5556YH (3) 86
       mm/sc
  6 34 implementation of integrated roadside vegetation plans.
  6 35    8.  Thirteen percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7  1 to support the following initiatives:
  7  2    a.  The maintenance and improvement of parks, preserves,
  7  3 wildlife areas, wildlife habitats, native prairies, and
  7  4 wetlands.
  7  5    b.  Wildlife diversity.
  7  6    c.  Recreational purposes.
  7  7    d.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  7  8    e.  Education and outreach programs and projects that provide
  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 14 to support initiatives related to the design, establishment,
  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.

  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 14 to support initiatives related to the design, establishment,
  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.
  7 22                           EXPLANATION
  7 23 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  7 24 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  7 25    This bill provides for an increase in the maximum local
  7 26 option sales tax rate to fund local natural resources and
  7 27 outdoor recreation projects.
  7 28    BACKGROUND.  Under current law, counties may impose a sales
  7 29 tax at the local level upon a petition of the voters or motions
  7 30 of city councils or the board of supervisors and after an
  7 31 election at which a majority of those voting favors imposition.
  7 32 A majority vote is also required for a repeal or rate change,
  7 33 but the governing body on its own motion may repeal the sales
  7 34 tax under certain circumstances.  The local option sales tax
  7 35 rate may not exceed one percent.
  8  1 Local option tax revenues collected in a county are remitted
  8  2 to the department of revenue (department) and, except for
  8  3 certain revenues attributable to urban renewal projects,
  8  4 distributed back to the county and cities within the county
  8  5 using a statutory formula involving population and historical
  8  6 property tax revenues.
  8  7    BILL CHANGES.  The bill increases the maximum local option
  8  8 sales tax rate that may be imposed by a county to one and
  8  9 three=eighths percent (1.375 percent) from one percent.  If a
  8 10 county votes to initially impose or to increase the tax rate
  8 11 above one percent, the bill requires tax revenues collected
  8 12 on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one percent to be
  8 13 remitted to counties and cities using the existing statutory
  8 14 formula, and then deposited in a special fund of the city or
  8 15 county and used exclusively for funding natural resources and
  8 16 outdoor recreation projects as described in the bill.
  8 17    The special fund moneys shall only be used to support
  8 18 voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for regulatory
  8 19 efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.  The bill allows
  8 20 for two or more cities or counties to enter into an agreement
  8 21 under Code chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  8 22 out any authorized initiative, and allows a city or county to
  8 23 deposit other local sales and services tax revenues it receives
  8 24 in its special natural resources and outdoor recreation fund.
  8 25    The bill also amends the calculation for determining
  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.
       LSB 5556YH (3) 86
       mm/sc
  7  7    d.  The improvement of water trails, rivers, and streams.
  7  8    e.  Education and outreach programs and projects that provide
  7  9 instruction regarding natural history and the outdoors. The
  7 10 subjects of such instruction may relate to opportunities
  7 11 involving recreational purposes, outdoor safety, and ethics.
  7 12    f.  Any other purpose described in section 350.1.
  7 13    9.  Ten percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 14 to support initiatives related to the design, establishment,
  7 15 maintenance, improvement, and expansion of land trails and
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.

  7 32 A majority vote is also required for a repeal or rate change,
  7 33 but the governing body on its own motion may repeal the sales
  7 34 tax under certain circumstances.  The local option sales tax
  7 35 rate may not exceed one percent.
  8  1 Local option tax revenues collected in a county are remitted
  8  2 to the department of revenue (department) and, except for
  8  3 certain revenues attributable to urban renewal projects,
  8  4 distributed back to the county and cities within the county
  8  5 using a statutory formula involving population and historical
  8  6 property tax revenues.
  8  7    BILL CHANGES.  The bill increases the maximum local option
  8  8 sales tax rate that may be imposed by a county to one and
  8  9 three=eighths percent (1.375 percent) from one percent.  If a
  8 10 county votes to initially impose or to increase the tax rate
  8 11 above one percent, the bill requires tax revenues collected
  8 12 on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one percent to be
  8 13 remitted to counties and cities using the existing statutory
  8 14 formula, and then deposited in a special fund of the city or
  8 15 county and used exclusively for funding natural resources and
  8 16 outdoor recreation projects as described in the bill.
  8 17    The special fund moneys shall only be used to support
  8 18 voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for regulatory
  8 19 efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.  The bill allows
  8 20 for two or more cities or counties to enter into an agreement
  8 21 under Code chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  8 22 out any authorized initiative, and allows a city or county to
  8 23 deposit other local sales and services tax revenues it receives
  8 24 in its special natural resources and outdoor recreation fund.
  8 25    The bill also amends the calculation for determining
  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.
       LSB 5556YH (3) 86
       mm/sc
  7 16 water trails.
  7 17    10.  Seven percent of the moneys in each fund shall be used
  7 18 to support public lake restoration initiatives.  An initiative
  7 19 shall account for a lake's recreational, environmental,
  7 20 aesthetic, ecological, and social value, and must improve water
  7 21 quality.
  7 22                           EXPLANATION
  7 23 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  7 24 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  7 25    This bill provides for an increase in the maximum local
  7 26 option sales tax rate to fund local natural resources and
  7 27 outdoor recreation projects.
  7 28    BACKGROUND.  Under current law, counties may impose a sales
  7 29 tax at the local level upon a petition of the voters or motions
  7 30 of city councils or the board of supervisors and after an
  7 31 election at which a majority of those voting favors imposition.
  7 32 A majority vote is also required for a repeal or rate change,
  7 33 but the governing body on its own motion may repeal the sales
  7 34 tax under certain circumstances.  The local option sales tax
  7 35 rate may not exceed one percent.
  8  1 Local option tax revenues collected in a county are remitted
  8  2 to the department of revenue (department) and, except for
  8  3 certain revenues attributable to urban renewal projects,
  8  4 distributed back to the county and cities within the county
  8  5 using a statutory formula involving population and historical
  8  6 property tax revenues.
  8  7    BILL CHANGES.  The bill increases the maximum local option
  8  8 sales tax rate that may be imposed by a county to one and
  8  9 three=eighths percent (1.375 percent) from one percent.  If a
  8 10 county votes to initially impose or to increase the tax rate
  8 11 above one percent, the bill requires tax revenues collected
  8 12 on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one percent to be
  8 13 remitted to counties and cities using the existing statutory
  8 14 formula, and then deposited in a special fund of the city or
  8 15 county and used exclusively for funding natural resources and
  8 16 outdoor recreation projects as described in the bill.
  8 17    The special fund moneys shall only be used to support
  8 18 voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for regulatory
  8 19 efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.  The bill allows
  8 20 for two or more cities or counties to enter into an agreement
  8 21 under Code chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  8 22 out any authorized initiative, and allows a city or county to
  8 23 deposit other local sales and services tax revenues it receives
  8 24 in its special natural resources and outdoor recreation fund.
  8 25    The bill also amends the calculation for determining
  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.

  8 16 outdoor recreation projects as described in the bill.
  8 17    The special fund moneys shall only be used to support
  8 18 voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for regulatory
  8 19 efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.  The bill allows
  8 20 for two or more cities or counties to enter into an agreement
  8 21 under Code chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  8 22 out any authorized initiative, and allows a city or county to
  8 23 deposit other local sales and services tax revenues it receives
  8 24 in its special natural resources and outdoor recreation fund.
  8 25    The bill also amends the calculation for determining
  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.
       LSB 5556YH (3) 86
       mm/sc
  7 27 outdoor recreation projects.
  7 28    BACKGROUND.  Under current law, counties may impose a sales
  7 29 tax at the local level upon a petition of the voters or motions
  7 30 of city councils or the board of supervisors and after an
  7 31 election at which a majority of those voting favors imposition.
  7 32 A majority vote is also required for a repeal or rate change,
  7 33 but the governing body on its own motion may repeal the sales
  7 34 tax under certain circumstances.  The local option sales tax
  7 35 rate may not exceed one percent.
  8  1 Local option tax revenues collected in a county are remitted
  8  2 to the department of revenue (department) and, except for
  8  3 certain revenues attributable to urban renewal projects,
  8  4 distributed back to the county and cities within the county
  8  5 using a statutory formula involving population and historical
  8  6 property tax revenues.
  8  7    BILL CHANGES.  The bill increases the maximum local option
  8  8 sales tax rate that may be imposed by a county to one and
  8  9 three=eighths percent (1.375 percent) from one percent.  If a
  8 10 county votes to initially impose or to increase the tax rate
  8 11 above one percent, the bill requires tax revenues collected
  8 12 on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one percent to be
  8 13 remitted to counties and cities using the existing statutory
  8 14 formula, and then deposited in a special fund of the city or
  8 15 county and used exclusively for funding natural resources and
  8 16 outdoor recreation projects as described in the bill.
  8 17    The special fund moneys shall only be used to support
  8 18 voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for regulatory
  8 19 efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.  The bill allows
  8 20 for two or more cities or counties to enter into an agreement
  8 21 under Code chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  8 22 out any authorized initiative, and allows a city or county to
  8 23 deposit other local sales and services tax revenues it receives
  8 24 in its special natural resources and outdoor recreation fund.
  8 25    The bill also amends the calculation for determining
  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.

  8 18 voluntary initiatives and shall not be used for regulatory
  8 19 efforts, enforcement actions, or litigation.  The bill allows
  8 20 for two or more cities or counties to enter into an agreement
  8 21 under Code chapter 28E to form an entity in order to carry
  8 22 out any authorized initiative, and allows a city or county to
  8 23 deposit other local sales and services tax revenues it receives
  8 24 in its special natural resources and outdoor recreation fund.
  8 25    The bill also amends the calculation for determining
  8 26 the funding of urban renewal projects to ensure that such
  8 27 calculation is not impacted by local option sales tax revenues
  8 28 collected on the amount of the tax rate in excess of one
  8 29 percent.
